## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor concentration ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the standard state variable in reaction-rate ODE models for homogeneous kinetics. With only t and A available, likely structures are rate laws where the instantaneous consumption/production rate depends on A (reaction order, saturation, inhibition) and possibly explicit time-dependence capturing changing conditions in a batch experiment.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption, e.g., surface-limited or excess-reactant regime)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order behavior)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or effective second-order decay)
- n-th order power-law kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall reaction order fitting)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type) kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with depletion/limiting concentration)
- Reversible first-order approach to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible nonlinear (cubic) stabilization: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) * (A**2 + c2) (equilibrium-seeking with stronger far-from-equilibrium pull)
- Rational saturation in A: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at high A due to limiting step/capacity)
- Substrate inhibition-like form: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A**2 + c1) (rate decreases at very high A due to self-inhibition/aggregation)
- Explicit time-dependent rate coefficient (exponential drift): dA_dt = -(c0 * exp(c1 * t)) * A (changing conditions over time; e.g., catalyst activation/deactivation or mixing/temperature drift)
- Explicit time-dependent rate coefficient (power drift): dA_dt = -(c0 * (t + c1)**c2) * A (time-varying effective first-order rate due to aging or ramped protocols)
- Biphasic/offset kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 (combined first-order decay plus baseline consumption/production offset)
- Oscillatory forcing of rate (periodic protocol): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (periodically modulated effective rate constant)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Straight-line in ln(A) vs t behavior suggests dA_dt proportional to A (first-order); ln(A) linearization is a key diagnostic.
- Curvature in 1/A vs t suggests dA_dt proportional to A**2 (second-order); reciprocal linearization checks this structure.
- Finite-time depletion with approximately linear A(t) suggests near-constant dA_dt (zero-order) until A becomes small.
- Approach to a nonzero plateau A → c1 suggests a restoring term (A - c1) in dA_dt, indicating equilibrium/steady-state rather than full depletion.
- Early-time acceleration of |dA_dt| as A increases (rather than decreases) suggests autocatalysis, often captured by A*(c1 - A) or A*(A - c1) forms.
- Rate that increases with A at low A but saturates at high A indicates a rational form in A such as A/(A + c1) (capacity-limited step).
- Rate that drops at very high A (after initially increasing) suggests self-inhibition/aggregation, often captured by denominators involving A**2 + c1 or higher powers.
- Systematic drift of apparent rate constant over time (same A gives different dA_dt at different t) suggests explicit k(t) multiplying an A-dependent law, e.g., exp(c*t) or (t+c)**c forms.
